The Superiority of Scholarly Jihad
Praise of scholarly jihad and its superiority over physical jihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers the intellectual jihad of scholars superior to physical jihad in preserving the religion.

Core Idea
Scholarly jihad preserves the eternal religion; physical jihad preserves temporary life and wealth.

In this powerful passage, the author defends the scholars of kalām by elevating their struggle against heretics above even the physical jihad of the sword. He argues that while physical jihad protects worldly life and property, the scholars' jihad safeguards the very religion whose loss leads to eternal damnation. This lesson explores that comparison and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the rhetorical questions
The author uses a series of rhetorical questions to build his argument. Pay attention to how each question reinforces the indispensability of scholars.
2
Identify the two types of jihad being compared
Find where he contrasts the scholars' use of proofs with the jihad of swords. Notice the criteria for superiority.
3
Understand the ultimate stakes
The author states that loss of religion leads to eternal hellfire, while loss of life and wealth is inevitable. This is the core of his argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهم المنزلة في الدنيا بحيث يتمكنونَ بها مِنْ سَوْقِ الناسِ إلى أغراضهم .. لولا ما نهضَ لهم رجالُ اللهِ مِنَ العلماء الراسخين ؟! وأي دين يبقى لعجوز أو صبي أو مُقلّد لولا بركةُ أولئكَ العلماءِ رضيَ اللهُ عنهم ؟! وأي جهادٍ يوازي جهادَ هؤلاء العلماء ؟! وأي رباط يماثلُ رباطهم وعكوفَهم على استعمال العقولِ وتحبيسِها مُدَّةَ الحياة على الجَوَلانِ فيما يحفظ دين المسلمين ؟! فمهما لاحَ لهم مُختلِسٌ يريدُ شيئاً مِنَ الدينِ . . قابلوه بشهابٍ مِنْ نَيْراتِ البراهين(١) ، فردُّوه خاسئاً لم ينقلب إلا بأعظم فضيحة ، وأينَ هذا الجهاد ورباطُهُ مِنْ جهادِ السيوف ورباط الثغور الذي غايتُهُ حفظ نفسٍ أو مالٍ لا بدَّ في الدنيا مِنْ فراقهما ، والأَوَّلُ حفظُ دين لو ذهب لهلك الناسُ في عذابِ جهنَّمَ أَبدَ الآبدين ؟! وقد رُوِيَ : أنَّ الأستاذ أبا إسحاق الإسفرايني رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ صَعِدَ في زمن هيجان المبتدعة إلى جبل لبنانَ ؛ وهو مُتعبدٌ لأولياء الله تعالى وخلوة لهم عن الناسِ ، فوجدَهم هنالك يتعبَّدونَ ، فقال لهم : يا أَكَلَةَ الحشيش ؛ هربتُم إلى هذا الموضع تتعبَّدون وتركتُم صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أيدي المبتدعة ؟! فقالوا له : أَيُّها الأستاذ ؛ لا قدرة لنا على مخالطة الخلق ، وأنت الذي أقدرَكَ اللهُ على ذلكَ ، فأنت أهله ، فرجع رضي الله عنه واشتغل بالرد على المبتدعة ، وأَلَّفَ كتابة ( الجامع بينَ الجلي والخفيّ ) ورُوِيَ : أَنَّ الأستاذ أبا بكرِ بنَ فُورَكَ لمَّا قرأَ مِنَ العلوم ما قُدِّرَ لهُ اعتزل عن الناس للعبادة ، فسمعَ هاتفاً يقولُ : الآنَ إِذْ صَرتَ حُجَّةً مِنْ حُجَج الله على خلقِهِ صرت تهربُ مِنَ الخلقِ ؟! فرجع إلى التعليم
And they have such status in the world that they are able to drive people towards their [i.e., religious] goals – were it not for the men of God, the firmly grounded scholars, rising up against them?! What religion would remain for an old woman, a boy, or a blind follower were it not for the blessing of those scholars, may God be pleased with them?! What jihad equals the jihad of these scholars?! What frontier-guarding (ribāṭ) matches their frontier-guarding and their devotion to employing the intellects and dedicating them for life to ranging over that which preserves the religion of the Muslims?! So whenever a thief appears to them wanting something of the religion, they meet him with a shooting star from the illuminating proofs, and they repel him, humiliated, and he returns only with the greatest disgrace. Where is this jihad and its frontier-guarding compared to the jihad of swords and the frontier-guarding of borders whose aim is the preservation of life or wealth – which inevitably must be parted with in this world – while the former is the preservation of a religion which, if lost, people would perish in the torment of Hell forever and ever?! It has been reported that the master Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī, may God be pleased with him, during a time of rampant innovation ascended Mount Lebanon – which was a place of worship for the saints of God Most High and a retreat for them away from people – and found them there worshipping. He said to them: 'O eaters of hashish! Have you fled to this place to worship and left the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, in the hands of the innovators?!' They said to him: 'O master, we have no ability to mix with people. You are the one God has empowered for that, so you are the one for it.' So he returned, may God be pleased with him, and occupied himself with refuting the innovators, and authored the book 'al-Jāmiʿ bayna al-Jalī wa al-Khafī'. And it is reported that the master Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak, after he had read such knowledge as was decreed for him, withdrew from people for worship. Then he heard a caller saying: 'Now that you have become a proof (ḥujjah) from among the proofs of God over His creation, you flee from creation?!' So he returned to teaching.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage defends the scholars of kalām (theologians) by asserting their immense status and the superiority of their intellectual jihad over physical jihad. The author begins by asking rhetorical questions emphasizing that without these scholars, no religion would remain for common people (old women, boys, blind followers). He then compares the scholars' jihad—using proofs to refute heretics—to physical jihad, concluding that the former is greater because it preserves religion, whose loss leads to eternal damnation. Two stories illustrate this: first, Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī rebukes ascetics who retreated to worship instead of defending the Prophet's teachings; they acknowledge his role and he returns to refute innovators. Second, Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak, after acquiring knowledge, withdraws for worship but is called back by a heavenly voice telling him he is now a proof of God and must engage with people. Both scholars exemplify the duty of defending the faith through teaching and argumentation.

Key Terms
جهاد
رباط
العلماء الراسخون
مبتدعة
براهين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Physical jihad is always superior to intellectual jihad.
Correction: The author argues that scholarly jihad is superior because it preserves the eternal religion, while physical jihad only protects temporary life and wealth.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the scholars' jihad superior to physical jihad?
A) Because it is harder
B) Because it preserves the religion, whose loss leads to eternal punishment
C) Because it involves swords
D) Because it is mentioned more in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The scholars' intellectual jihad is superior to physical jihad because it preserves the religion for eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you like the 'old woman, boy, or blind follower' who would have no religion were it not for the scholars? What are you actively doing to become a firmly grounded person instead of a passive recipient?
?
The scholars dedicate their intellects 'for life' to preserve the religion. You will stand before Allah and be asked: What did you do with your mental energy? Did you ever defend your faith with knowledge, or did you let it be stolen by every doubt or cross?
?
Tomorrow, when you are parted from your life and wealth—which physical jihad protects—what will remain of your deeds? If your religion is lost due to ignorance or neglect, how will you answer the One who gave it to you?

The Call to Defend the Faith: Al-Isfarayini
Story of al-Isfarayini's return from retreat to defend the faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Isfarayini was drawn from ascetic retreat to actively refuting innovators.

Core Idea
True scholars cannot abandon the community to defend the faith.

This story of Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī illustrates the duty of scholars to engage in defending the faith rather than retreating into pure worship. When he finds ascetics hiding in Mount Lebanon, he rebukes them for leaving the Prophet's teachings vulnerable to innovators. This lesson follows his journey from retreat to active refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the story and identify the setting
Notice that al-Isfarayini goes to Mount Lebanon during a time of rampant innovation.
2
Understand his rebuke
He calls the ascetics 'eaters of hashish' for fleeing worship while leaving the Prophet in the hands of innovators.
3
See the response and his action
The ascetics acknowledge his capability, and he returns to write a book against innovation.

?

?

From Retreat to Teaching: Ibn Furak
Story of Ibn Furak's return to teaching upon hearing a heavenly voice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the call for a scholar to return to teaching after acquiring knowledge.

Core Idea
A scholar becomes a proof of God and must engage with people.

This brief story of Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak shows that after gaining deep knowledge, a scholar cannot withdraw from the community. A heavenly voice reminds him that he is now one of God's proofs upon creation and must not flee from people. This lesson highlights the responsibility that comes with knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the story and note Ibn Furak's initial action
After acquiring knowledge, he withdrew from people to worship.
2
Identify the heavenly caller's message
The caller says: 'Now that you have become a proof (ḥujjah) from God's proofs, you flee from creation?'
3
Understand his response
He returns to teaching, fulfilling his duty.

ولهم المنزلة في الدنيا بحيث يتمكنونَ بها مِنْ سَوْقِ الناسِ إلى أغراضهم .. لولا ما نهضَ لهم رجالُ اللهِ مِنَ العلماء الراسخين ؟! وأي دين يبقى لعجوز أو صبي أو مُقلّد لولا بركةُ أولئكَ العلماءِ رضيَ اللهُ عنهم ؟! وأي جهادٍ يوازي جهادَ هؤلاء العلماء ؟! وأي رباط يماثلُ رباطهم وعكوفَهم على استعمال العقولِ وتحبيسِها مُدَّةَ الحياة على الجَوَلانِ فيما يحفظ دين المسلمين ؟! فمهما لاحَ لهم مُختلِسٌ يريدُ شيئاً مِنَ الدينِ . . قابلوه بشهابٍ مِنْ نَيْراتِ البراهين(١) ، فردُّوه خاسئاً لم ينقلب إلا بأعظم فضيحة ، وأينَ هذا الجهاد ورباطُهُ مِنْ جهادِ السيوف ورباط الثغور الذي غايتُهُ حفظ نفسٍ أو مالٍ لا بدَّ في الدنيا مِنْ فراقهما ، والأَوَّلُ حفظُ دين لو ذهب لهلك الناسُ في عذابِ جهنَّمَ أَبدَ الآبدين ؟! وقد رُوِيَ : أنَّ الأستاذ أبا إسحاق الإسفرايني رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ صَعِدَ في زمن هيجان المبتدعة إلى جبل لبنانَ ؛ وهو مُتعبدٌ لأولياء الله تعالى وخلوة لهم عن الناسِ ، فوجدَهم هنالك يتعبَّدونَ ، فقال لهم : يا أَكَلَةَ الحشيش ؛ هربتُم إلى هذا الموضع تتعبَّدون وتركتُم صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أيدي المبتدعة ؟! فقالوا له : أَيُّها الأستاذ ؛ لا قدرة لنا على مخالطة الخلق ، وأنت الذي أقدرَكَ اللهُ على ذلكَ ، فأنت أهله ، فرجع رضي الله عنه واشتغل بالرد على المبتدعة ، وأَلَّفَ كتابة ( الجامع بينَ الجلي والخفيّ ) ورُوِيَ : أَنَّ الأستاذ أبا بكرِ بنَ فُورَكَ لمَّا قرأَ مِنَ العلوم ما قُدِّرَ لهُ اعتزل عن الناس للعبادة ، فسمعَ هاتفاً يقولُ : الآنَ إِذْ صَرتَ حُجَّةً مِنْ حُجَج الله على خلقِهِ صرت تهربُ مِنَ الخلقِ ؟! فرجع إلى التعليم
And they have such status in the world that they are able to drive people towards their [i.e., religious] goals – were it not for the men of God, the firmly grounded scholars, rising up against them?! What religion would remain for an old woman, a boy, or a blind follower were it not for the blessing of those scholars, may God be pleased with them?! What jihad equals the jihad of these scholars?! What frontier-guarding (ribāṭ) matches their frontier-guarding and their devotion to employing the intellects and dedicating them for life to ranging over that which preserves the religion of the Muslims?! So whenever a thief appears to them wanting something of the religion, they meet him with a shooting star from the illuminating proofs, and they repel him, humiliated, and he returns only with the greatest disgrace. Where is this jihad and its frontier-guarding compared to the jihad of swords and the frontier-guarding of borders whose aim is the preservation of life or wealth – which inevitably must be parted with in this world – while the former is the preservation of a religion which, if lost, people would perish in the torment of Hell forever and ever?! It has been reported that the master Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī, may God be pleased with him, during a time of rampant innovation ascended Mount Lebanon – which was a place of worship for the saints of God Most High and a retreat for them away from people – and found them there worshipping. He said to them: 'O eaters of hashish! Have you fled to this place to worship and left the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, in the hands of the innovators?!' They said to him: 'O master, we have no ability to mix with people. You are the one God has empowered for that, so you are the one for it.' So he returned, may God be pleased with him, and occupied himself with refuting the innovators, and authored the book 'al-Jāmiʿ bayna al-Jalī wa al-Khafī'. And it is reported that the master Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak, after he had read such knowledge as was decreed for him, withdrew from people for worship. Then he heard a caller saying: 'Now that you have become a proof (ḥujjah) from among the proofs of God over His creation, you flee from creation?!' So he returned to teaching.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage defends the scholars of kalām (theologians) by asserting their immense status and the superiority of their intellectual jihad over physical jihad. The author begins by asking rhetorical questions emphasizing that without these scholars, no religion would remain for common people (old women, boys, blind followers). He then compares the scholars' jihad—using proofs to refute heretics—to physical jihad, concluding that the former is greater because it preserves religion, whose loss leads to eternal damnation. Two stories illustrate this: first, Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī rebukes ascetics who retreated to worship instead of defending the Prophet's teachings; they acknowledge his role and he returns to refute innovators. Second, Abū Bakr ibn Fūrak, after acquiring knowledge, withdraws for worship but is called back by a heavenly voice telling him he is now a proof of God and must engage with people. Both scholars exemplify the duty of defending the faith through teaching and argumentation.

حجة

The Obligation of Teaching: The Story of Ibn Furak
Sanusi narrates a story about Ibn Furak being called back to teaching after seclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand from the story of Ibn Furak that knowledge obligates teaching and that seclusion is not justified for one who can guide others.

Core Idea
Knowledge becomes a duty to teach.

This lesson presents a brief but powerful anecdote from the life of the great Ash'ari scholar Abu Bakr ibn Furak. After completing his studies, he withdrew for worship, but a supernatural voice called him back, reminding him that his knowledge made him a proof of God. The story underscores that scholarship carries a responsibility to guide others.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the sequence: study, seclusion, call, return.
Pay attention to the precise wording of the rebuke.
2

The term 'hātif' refers to a supernatural voice.
3
Reflect on the lesson

Consider the balance between personal devotion and communal responsibility.
4
Examine the common misunderstanding
Some think seclusion for worship is always better. This story shows that teaching is a duty for scholars.
The story directly corrects that misconception.

Commentary

A supernatural voice (hātif) rebuked him: when he became a proof (ḥujjah) of God, he should not abandon the people. The point is that knowledge obligates teaching; retreat is not justified when one can guide others.

Ali's Spontaneous Knowledge and the Pulpit Inheritance
Praises Ali's knowledge and gives the pulpit inheritance example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the extraordinary depth of Ali's knowledge as demonstrated by his immediate solution to the complex inheritance problem known as the Pulpit Inheritance.

Core Idea
Ali's knowledge turned impossible fractions into simple answers instantly.

This passage from Sanusi's text highlights the unparalleled knowledge of Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA). It presents him as the gate to the city of prophetic knowledge, capable of resolving the most intricate legal problems without hesitation. The focal example is the famous 'Pulpit Inheritance' problem, where Ali's immediate answer transformed a seemingly impossible fraction into a workable solution, showing the depth of his understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the author builds from general praise to a specific example.
2
Identify the claims about Ali's knowledge
Find the hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate' and the statement about placing the weight of seventy camels on al-Fatiha. These establish Ali's unparalleled knowledge.
3
Understand the inheritance problem
The problem involves a wife, two daughters, and both parents. Normally, the shares add up to more than the estate, requiring adjustment. Ali's response 'Its eighth became a ninth' shows he knew the adjusted share immediately.
This is a well-known case in Islamic inheritance law called 'awl' (adjustment).
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author highlights this example. It demonstrates that Ali's knowledge was not merely academic but intuitive and immediate, even in high-pressure situations like on the pulpit.

رضي الله عنهم أو صبي مُميَّز مِنْ صبيانهم ، وكذا التابعون وتابعوهم بإحسان . ولقد أدرك علي رضي الله عنه زمنَ المبتدعة ، وأفحمهم بما لم يقدروا أن يجدوا معه جواباً ، وحُكِيَ عنه رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ أَنَّهُ قالَ : ( لو أذنَ لي رسولُ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ أضعَ على « الفاتحةِ » وِقْرَ سبعين بعيراً.. لفعلتُ ) ، وقالَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَنَا مَدِينَةُ الْعِلْمِ وَعَلِيٌّ بَابُهَا ) ، وقد نُقِلَ عنه رضي الله عنه في كل علم العجب العُجاب ، حتى افتتنت بهِ طوائفُ مِنَ المبتدعة وادَّعى بعضُهم فيهِ ما ادَّعَتْهُ النصارى في عيسى عليه السلام . ومن عجيبِ أمرِه رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : أَنَّ مُعضلاتِ المسائل التي لا يُتوصل إلى جوابها إلا بالأنظارِ الدقيقة في السنين المتطاولة .. إذا سُئِلَ هو عنها أجابَ عنها بديهةً مِنْ غيرِ تأمل ولا تعظيم لشأنها ، كأنَّها عنده سؤال الأمور الضرورية ؛ ككون الاثنين مثلاً أكثرَ مِنَ الواحد ، وقضاياه في ذلك مشهورةٌ مسطورةٌ في الكُتُب ، وتأمل جوابه رضي الله عنه على المنبر في الفريضة المنبرية ؛ وهي : زوجة وابنتان وأبوان ، وقوله على البديهة بلا تأمل ولا تأخُرٍ في ذلك الموقفِ الصعب : ( صارَ ثُمنُها تسعاً ) ، ثم اعرض على عقول أكثر الناسِ ذلك وانظر أين هم ممَّا هنالك
May Allah be pleased with them or a discerning child from their children, and likewise the Followers and those who followed them in goodness. And indeed Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, encountered the time of the innovators and silenced them with what they could not find an answer to. And it is related from him, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'If the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, had permitted me to place upon the Fatiha the load of seventy camels... I would have done so.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate.' And it has been transmitted from him, may Allah be pleased with him, in every branch of knowledge the most wondrous marvels, until sects of innovators were seduced by him and some of them claimed concerning him what the Christians claimed concerning Jesus, peace be upon him. And among the wondrous matters of his, may Allah be pleased with him: that complex questions which are not reached except by precise reflections over many years - if he was asked about them, he would answer them spontaneously without pondering or deeming them significant, as if they were for him like questions about necessary matters, such as that two is more than one. And his judgments in that are famous and recorded in books. And contemplate his answer, may Allah be pleased with him, on the pulpit concerning the pulpit inheritance division: which is a wife, two daughters, and both parents, and his statement spontaneously without reflection or delay in that difficult situation: 'Its eighth became a ninth.' Then present that to the minds of most people and see where they are from that.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section extolling the knowledge of Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA). The author first notes that Ali confronted the innovators and silenced them irrefutably. A quote is given where Ali states that had the Prophet permitted, he would have placed the weight of seventy camels worth of meaning on Surah al-Fatiha. Then the famous hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate' is cited. The author remarks that Ali was so knowledgeable that some extremists exaggerated him like Christians exaggerated Jesus. Then the author describes a remarkable trait: Ali could answer the most difficult questions instantly, without reflection, as if they were self-evident. The example given is the 'fardah minbariyyah' (pulpit inheritance problem) involving a wife, two daughters, and both parents. Ali's immediate answer was that the wife's share changes from 1/8 to 1/9. This is a well-known issue in inheritance law where the shares exceed the total, requiring an adjustment (awl). The author challenges the reader to appreciate the depth of Ali's spontaneous response.

Ali's Mathematical Resolution of the Bread Dispute
The author narrates Ali's spontaneous calculation to divide a gift fairly between two companions who shared bread with a stranger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali (ra) resolved a complex dispute over bread sharing using a mathematical calculation based on equal consumption.

Core Idea
Ali's spontaneous calculation transformed a contentious dispute into a lesson of precise justice.

This passage narrates a famous incident from the life of Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra), showcasing his remarkable ability to solve disputes with instant mathematical reasoning. Two men shared their bread with a stranger, and when compensated, they argued over how to split the payment. Ali's solution, produced on the spot, demonstrates both his intellectual genius and his commitment to true justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the narrative. Notice the initial situation, the dispute, and Ali's intervention.
The calculation is complex, so focus on the sequence first.
2
Identify the dispute
Two men had 3 and 5 loaves respectively. A traveler joined, they ate all 8 loaves together. Then the traveler gave 8 dirhams. One man wanted equal split (4 each), the other wanted proportional to loaves (3 and 5).
The first man swore to accept only true justice.
3
Understand Ali's calculation
Ali assumed each person ate equally (8/3 loaves). He multiplied total loaves (8) by number of eaters (3) to get 24 as a base. Then for each man, he multiplied his loaves by 3, subtracted his own consumption (8), getting net contribution: 1 for the first, 7 for the second.
Thus the first gets 1 dirham, the second gets 7 dirhams.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ali's method ensures fairness based on what each actually contributed after eating. This incident highlights Ali's wisdom and the importance of justice in Islamic teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك فتواه في رجلين ؛ لأحدهما ثلاثة أرغفة ، وللآخرِ خمسة ، هجم عليهما ثالثُ ، فقدَّما لهُ ما معهما ، واستوعبوا ثلاثتهم ذلكَ أَكْلاً ، فلما قامَ عنهما أجازهما بثمانية دراهم ، فقال صاحب الثلاثة : هي بيننا نصفين ، وقالَ الآخرُ : بل على عدد أرغفة كلِّ واحدٍ ، فحلف الأوَّلُ ألا يأخذ إلا ما أعطاه صميم الحقِّ ، فرفعه إلى علي رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : خُذْ ما أعطاك ، فقالَ : إن كان بصميم الحقِّ ، فقال علي رضي الله عنه بديهةً : إذا ليس لك إلا درهم واحدٌ فقال : كيف ؟ فقال : أكلتُم ثلاثتُكم ثمانية أرغفة ، وقَدْرُ ما أكل كلٌّ منكم غير معلوم ، فتحملون على السواء ، وثمانية على ثلاثتكم تباينها ، فتُضرَبُ فيها ، فتصيرُ أربعة وعشرينَ ، تُضرَبُ أرغفة كلِّ منكما فيما ضُرِبَتْ فيهِ الثمانيةُ المجموع ، فلك ثلاثةٌ ، تُضرَبُ في الثلاثةِ التي ضُرِبَتْ فيها الثمانيةُ ، فذلك تسعة ، أكلت منها ثمانية بقي لك واحد ، ولصاحبك خمسةٌ ، تُضرَبُ له في الثلاثةِ ، فذلك خمسة عشر ، أكل منها ثمانية وبقي له سبعةٌ ، فقد أكل لكَ الوارد جزءاً ، ولصاحبك سبعةً ، وإنَّما وهبكما لذلك ، فاقسما ما منحكما على قَدْرِ ما منحتماه
And similarly his legal opinion concerning two men: one of them had three loaves, and the other five. A third man joined them, so they presented to him what they had, and all three of them ate that completely. When he left them, he gave them eight dirhams. The owner of three loaves said: 'Let it be split between us equally.' The other said: 'Rather, according to the number of loaves of each one.' The first swore that he would not take except what true justice gave him, so he brought the case to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him. He said: 'Take what he gave you.' He said: 'Only if it is true justice.' So Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, said spontaneously: 'Then you have only one dirham.' He said: 'How?' He said: 'You three ate eight loaves, and the amount each of you ate is unknown, so you assume equality. Multiply eight by three, it becomes twenty-four. Multiply the loaves of each of you by what the total eight was multiplied by. Yours is three, multiplied by three (which eight was multiplied by), that is nine. You ate eight of them, leaving you one. Your companion has five, multiplied by three, that is fifteen. He ate eight, leaving him seven. So the attendant ate one part from you and seven from your companion, and indeed he gifted you both for that. So divide what he gave you according to what you gave him.'
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage narrates a famous incident showcasing Ali's ability to solve a dispute instantly with mathematical precision. Two men shared their bread (3 and 5 loaves) with a third traveler. After eating all 8 loaves equally (assuming each ate 8/3 loaves), the traveler gave 8 dirhams as compensation. The dispute was over dividing the 8 dirhams: the first wanted equal split (4 each), the second wanted proportional split (3:5 -> 3 and 5). They went to Ali, who first told the first man to accept the offered 4 (the equal split?), but the man insisted on exact justice. Ali then calculated: total loaves 8, total eaters 3, assume equal consumption. Multiply total loaves by number of eaters (8×3=24) to get a common base. Each man's 'contribution' after consumption is: for the first, his 3 loaves multiplied by 3 = 9, minus his own consumption (8) = 1 dirham of net contribution. For the second, 5×3=15 minus 8 = 7 dirhams. Thus the first gets 1 dirham, the second gets 7 dirhams. This is a complex calculation (using the method of areas) that Ali produced spontaneously on the spot, demonstrating his intellectual genius.

Key Terms
أرغفة
بديهة
صميم الحق
ضرب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ali's solution was arbitrary or unfair, favoring the one with more loaves.
Correction: Ali's calculation is mathematically sound: it accounts for equal consumption and divides compensation based on net contribution, ensuring true justice.

Checkpoint
According to Ali's calculation, how many dirhams did the owner of three loaves receive?
A) 4
B) 3
C) 1
D) 5

Key Takeaway
Ali's spontaneous calculation demonstrates that true justice requires accounting for both contribution and consumption, not just initial shares.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The first man swore he would accept nothing less than 'true justice', even if it meant receiving only one dirham instead of four. Is your commitment to justice that strong when you stand to lose? Would you walk away from a perceived gain for the sake of what is truly fair?
?
Ali (ra) spontaneously produced a mathematically complete solution. When you face a complex disagreement, do you rush to a quick, self-serving resolution, or do you pause and seek the deeper fairness that may require sacrifice from you?
?
The traveler's gift was a blessing from Allah. The men divided it based on what they gave, not what they expected. When you receive a blessing (money, praise, opportunity), do you measure it by your contribution or by your entitlement?

Ali's Judgment on the Loaves Dispute
Ali resolves a dispute over bread sharing with a mathematical calculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali (ra) applied a fair and precise mathematical calculation to resolve a dispute over bread sharing, based on equity and unknown individual consumption.

Core Idea
True justice requires precise calculation, not just equal division.

This passage recounts a famous incident from the life of Ali ibn Abi Talib, illustrating his remarkable wisdom in dispute resolution. The story involves two men who shared their loaves with a third traveler, and the subsequent disagreement over how to divide the traveler's payment. Through a brilliant mathematical insight, Ali determined the exact amount each was entitled to, demonstrating that divine justice is both ethical and exact.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic story and translation to understand the context and the dispute. Note the characters: the two owners (3 and 5 loaves), the visitor, and the claims.
The story is a famous example of Ali's quick judgment.
2
Identify the problem
Two men disagreed on how to split the 8 dirhams: one said equally (4 each), the other said proportionally to loaves contributed (3:5). The first man swore to take only what is purely just.
3
Understand Ali's initial response
Ali first said 'Take what he gave you,' suggesting acceptance. But when the man insisted on pure truth, Ali gave a different answer.
This shows Ali's depth of knowledge; he had a quick calculation ready.
4
Follow the calculation
Trace Ali's reasoning: assume equal eating (each ate 8/3 loaves). Multiply loaves by 3 to avoid fractions. Compute net contribution: owner of 3 loaves gave 1 part, owner of 5 gave 7 parts. Hence 1 dirham vs 7 dirhams.
The key is the assumption of equal consumption.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how Ali's judgment exemplifies fairness and the role of knowledge in Islamic jurisprudence. It shows that justice sometimes requires unconventional methods.
This story is often cited to highlight Ali's intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك فتواه في رجلين ؛ لأحدهما ثلاثة أرغفة ، وللآخرِ خمسة ، هجم عليهما ثالثُ ، فقدَّما لهُ ما معهما ، واستوعبوا ثلاثتهم ذلكَ أَكْلاً ، فلما قامَ عنهما أجازهما بثمانية دراهم(۱) ، فقال صاحب الثلاثة : هي بيننا نصفين ، وقالَ الآخرُ : بل على عدد أرغفة كلَّ واحدٍ ، فحلف الأوَّلُ ألا يأخذ إلا ما أعطاه صميم الحقِّ ، فرفعه إلى علي رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : خُذْ ما أعطاك ، فقالَ : إِنْ كانَ إِنْ كَانَ بصميمِ الحقِّ ، فقال علي رضي الله عنه بديهةً : إذا ليس لك إلا درهم واحدٌ فقال : كيف ؟ فقال : أكلتُم ثلاثتُكم ثمانية أرغفة ، وقَدْرُ ما أكل كلٌّ منكم غير معلوم ، فتحملون على السواء ، وثمانية على ثلاثتكم تباينها ، فتُضرَبُ فيها ، فتصيرُ أربعة وعشرينَ ، تُضرَبُ أرغفة كلَّ منكما فيما ضُرِبَتْ فيهِ الثمانيةُ المجموع ، فلك ثلاثةٌ ، تُضرَبُ في الثلاثةِ التي ضُرِبَتْ فيها الثمانيةُ ، فذلك تسعة ، أكلت منها ثمانية بقي لك واحد ، ولصاحبك خمسةٌ ، تُضرَبُ له في الثلاثةِ ، فذلك خمسة عشر ، أكل منها ثمانية وبقي له سبعةٌ ، فقد أكل لكَ الوارد جزءاً ، ولصاحبك سبعةً ، وإِنَّما وهبكما لذلك ، فاقسما ما منحكما على قَدْرِ ما منحتماه
And likewise his ruling concerning two men: one had three loaves, and the other had five. A third man attacked [i.e., joined] them, and they presented to him what they had, and the three of them consumed that completely. When he [the third] left them, he rewarded them with eight dirhams. The owner of the three loaves said: 'It is between us equally.' The other said: 'Rather, according to the number of loaves of each one.' The first one swore that he would not take except what the pure truth gave him. So he referred it to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him. He said: 'Take what he gave you.' He said: 'If it was according to the pure truth…' So Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, said instantly: 'Then you have nothing except one dirham.' He said: 'How?' He said: 'You three ate eight loaves, and the amount that each of you ate is unknown, so it is to be assumed equal. Eight over your three: it is not divisible, so multiply it into them, so it becomes twenty-four. Multiply the loaves of each of you by that which the eight were multiplied. For you: three loaves multiplied by the three that the eight were multiplied by — that is nine; you ate eight of them, so one remains for you. For your companion: five loaves multiplied by the three — that is fifteen; he ate eight of them, so seven remain for him. So the visitor ate from you one part and from your companion seven parts. And indeed he rewarded you for that, so divide what he gave you according to what you gave him.'
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a historical anecdote illustrating Caliph Ali's immediate and precise judgment in a dispute over shared food and payment. The story: two men had three and five loaves respectively. A third man joined them, and they all ate the eight loaves together. The visitor later gave them eight dirhams as compensation. One claimant demanded an equal split (4 each), the other demanded a proportional split based on loaves contributed. The first claimant swore to take only what was purely just. Ali first said 'Take what he gave you,' but when the man insisted on pure justice, Ali instantly calculated a different distribution: only 1 dirham for the owner of three loaves, 7 for the owner of five. Ali's reasoning: since the amount each ate is unknown, assume they ate equally. Each person's share of the eight loaves is 8/3 of a loaf. But the two men originally contributed 3 and 5 loaves. To find net contribution after eating, multiply each loaf count by the factor 3 (since 8 loaves × 3 = 24 total shares). Owner of 3 loaves contributed 9 shares; he ate 8, so he effectively gave 1 to the visitor. Owner of 5 loaves contributed 15 shares; he ate 8, so he gave 7 to the visitor. Hence the visitor's reward should be split 1:7. The passage shows Ali's profound knowledge and quick reasoning in applying equity.

Key Terms
بديهةً
صميم الحق
فتوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's judgment was arbitrary or emotional.
Correction: Ali's judgment was a precise mathematical calculation based on equity and the assumption of equal eating.

Checkpoint
Why did Ali award only 1 dirham to the owner of three loaves?
A) Because he ate more than his share
B) Because after equal eating assumption, he contributed only 1 loaf net to the visitor
C) Because the other man was more deserving
D) Because the visitor had a claim

Key Takeaway
Ali's judgment demonstrates that Islamic justice requires precise fairness rooted in careful reasoning and mathematical equity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in a conflict over resources, do you insist on 'your right' without first calculating what you truly deserve? Could you, like the first man, swear to take only what is purely just—even if it means getting less than you thought?
?
Ali calculated that the man who contributed more also consumed the same amount, so his net gift was larger. In your own relationships, do you give more than you take? Or do you keep score? How would your life change if you gave without expecting reward, trusting in Allah's justice?
?
The visitor rewarded them with eight dirhams based on their apparent contribution, but Ali revealed a deeper justice. When you receive blessings from others, do you look only at the surface or try to understand the deeper fairness? How can you apply this principle of precise equity in your daily dealings?

Ali's Instant Inheritance Verdict
Ali instantly identifies the correct heirs from a woman's complaint.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's immediate knowledge of inheritance shares confirmed the justice of a seemingly unfair distribution.

Core Idea
Justice in inheritance is not always equal—Ali's instant calculation proves it.

The story of a grieving woman who received only one dirham from her brother's estate might seem like an injustice. But when she brought her complaint to Ali, he immediately identified the likely heirs and assured her that her share was correct. This anecdote showcases Ali's mastery of Islamic inheritance law (fara'id) and the importance of understanding the distribution rules before judging fairness.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Pay attention to the flow: the woman's complaint, Ali's response, and the final verdict.
Notice that Ali does not hesitate—he answers 'immediately'.
2
Identify the listed heirs
Ali lists: wife, mother, two daughters, and twelve brothers. Consider how many heirs are involved and how that might affect the woman's share.
The woman is a sister; with so many heirs, her share becomes very small.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: Why is this story important? It demonstrates that the caliph had deep knowledge of Islamic law and that apparent injustice can be legally correct.
This builds trust in the leadership and the legal system.

Commentary
This passage is another anecdote demonstrating Ali's immediate knowledge of Islamic inheritance law (fara'id). A woman complained that her brother died leaving 600 dirhams, but she received only one dirham. Without hesitation, Ali described the potential heirs: wife, mother, two daughters, and twelve brothers. When she confirmed, he stated that her share of one dirham was correct. The implication is that under such a distribution, the woman's share (as a sister) would indeed be small. The story highlights Ali's ability to recall complex inheritance rules instantly and reassure the woman that no injustice occurred.

Umar's Knowledge and Spiritual Unveiling
Author demonstrates Umar's superior knowledge through hadith and kashf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sources that demonstrate Umar ibn al-Khattab's extraordinary knowledge and the concept of spiritual unveiling (kashf).

Core Idea
Umar's knowledge was divinely inspired, surpassing ordinary learning.

This lesson explores the profound knowledge of Umar ibn al-Khattab as attested by Ali ibn Abi Talib, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, and a prophetic dream. The passage also introduces the concept of kashf (unveiling), where Umar's pure mind received knowledge directly from Allah. By examining these testimonies, we gain insight into the spiritual stature of one of Islam's greatest figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow.
Notice the three distinct testimonies and the final description of Umar.
2
Identify the three proofs
Identify the statements from Ali, Sa'id, and the hadith. Understand how each supports Umar's superior knowledge.
The dream interpretation is key—milk symbolizing knowledge.
3
Understand kashf (unveiling)
Reflect on the term 'mukkashaf' and how Umar's pure mind could inscribe knowledge without external evidence.
Kashf is a form of divine inspiration beyond ordinary learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هو معَ هذا كلّهِ كانَ يقولُ في عمرَ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ لَمَّا ماتَ : مات أعرفنا بالله تعالى وقال سعيدُ بنُ المسيَّبِ : ما رأيتُ أعرفُ مِنْ عمر ، وفي الصحيح » : أنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ رأى أنه يشربُ لبناً حتى كاد الرَّيُّ يخرجُ مِنْ أَظفارِهِ ، وأعطى فضلةَ ذلكَ اللبن لعمرَ ، وأوَّلَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ تلك الرؤيا بالعلم (۳) . وكانَ عمرُ رضي الله عنهُ مكاشفاً ، لا يُقدِّرُ بذهنِهِ شيئاً إِلا كَانَ فإذا كان يرتسم في مرآةِ ذهنِهِ الصافية ما لا دليل عليهِ ولا أَمارة . .
Then he [Ali], with all this, used to say about Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he died: 'He died the most knowledgeable of us about Allah the Exalted.' And Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib said: 'I have not seen anyone more knowledgeable than Umar.' And in the Sahih: that the Prophet, peace be upon him, saw in a dream that he was drinking milk until satiation almost came out from his fingernails, and he gave the remainder of that milk to Umar. And the Prophet interpreted that dream as knowledge. And Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, was a mukkashaf (one who experiences unveiling); he would not conceive of anything in his mind except that it was as if it were becoming inscribed in the mirror of his pure mind with no evidence or indication.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage establishes the extraordinary knowledge of Umar ibn al-Khattab. It begins by quoting Ali's testimony that Umar was 'the most knowledgeable of us about Allah' at his death. Then Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib confirms his unparalleled knowledge. The author then cites a hadith from the Sahih (Bukhari and Muslim): the Prophet dreamed he was drinking milk until satiation came from his fingernails, and he gave the leftover to Umar; the Prophet interpreted this dream as 'knowledge.' Thus Umar received prophetic knowledge symbolically. Finally, the author describes Umar as 'mukkashaf' (one granted unveiling), meaning his mind was so pure that whatever he thought would become manifest, even without external evidence. This emphasizes that Umar's knowledge was divinely inspired.

الرؤيا
العلم
مرآة الذهن

Correction: The hadith and description indicate that Umar's knowledge was divinely inspired through prophecy and unveiling (kashf).

Key Takeaway

Umar's Exceptional Knowledge and Unshakeable Certainty
Anecdotal demonstration of Umar's intuitive knowledge and certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Umar ibn al-Khattab's extraordinary knowledge of Allah exemplifies the highest levels of marifa and yaqin, and how his intuitive perception stemmed from deep immersion in revelation.

Core Idea
Umar's knowledge of Allah was so deep it became part of his very being.

This passage from a classical text celebrates the unique spiritual stature of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Through anecdotes and prophetic testimonies, it reveals how his intellect was elevated to the level of unveiling (kashf), making theoretical knowledge intuitive and certainty absolute. As we read, we will see how Umar's trust in his God-given intellect allowed him to face even the angels of the grave with complete confidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm and the stories come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's use of rhetorical questions to emphasize Umar's status.
2
Identify the key stories
The passage presents several stories about Umar: the inheritance calculation, the dream of milk, the grave questioning, and a brief mention of Uthman. Note what each story demonstrates about Umar's knowledge or certainty.
3
Reflect on 'holy perception'
The author describes Umar's 'holy perception' (إدراك قدسي) that made theoretical sciences necessary for him. Ask yourself how this relates to the process of gaining knowledge of Allah through proofs.
This concept is central to understanding Umar's intuitive grasp of difficult matters.
4
Analyze the grave incident
Focus on Umar's question about his intellect being with him and his confident response. Consider what this reveals about his level of certainty (yaqin).
The Prophet's affirmation 'Indeed, Umar is certain' is a key testimony.

Connect to the theme of knowledge of Allah
The author argues that if Umar had such perception in worldly matters, his knowledge of Allah must be profound. Reflect on how the stories collectively support this claim.

ثم هو معَ هذا كلّهِ كانَ يقولُ في عمرَ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ لَمَّا ماتَ : مات أعرفنا بالله تعالى وقال سعيدُ بنُ المسيَّبِ : ما رأيتُ أعرفُ مِنْ عمر ، وفي الصحيح » : أنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ رأى أنه يشربُ لبناً حتى كاد الرَّيُّ يخرجُ مِنْ أَظفارِهِ ، وأعطى فضلةَ ذلكَ اللبن لعمرَ ، وأوَّلَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ تلك الرؤيا بالعلم (٣) . وكانَ عمرُ رضي الله عنهُ مكاشفاً ، لا يُقدِّرُ بذهنِهِ شيئاً إِلا كَانَ فإذا كان يرتسم في مرآةِ ذهنِهِ الصافية ما لا دليل عليهِ ولا أَمارة . . فكيف يكون ذهنه لمعرفةِ مَنِ الكائنات كلُّها مُطبقةٌ على واضح الدلالةِ عليه جل وعزَّ ؟! وانظر قولَهُ رضي الله عنهُ لمَّا أخبره النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بفتنةِ القبرِ وسؤال الملكين وصفتهما ، فقال : أيكونُ معي عقلي فقالَ : « نَعَمْ نَعَمْ » ، فقال : إذاً أكفيكَهما ، فقال النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( إِنَّ عُمَرَ لَمُوقِنٌ (١) . « فانظر إلى وثوقِهِ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ بنظرِ عقلِهِ وعدم اكتراثه بمناظرةِ مَنْ علمه مترقٌ عن علم اليقين إلى عين اليقين ؛ وهم الملائكةُ ، ولم يخف أن يشغل فكرَهُ هولُ منظرهما ، ولا فظاعة القبرِ الذي هو أوَّلُ منزلٍ مِنْ منازل الآخرة ، وهل تصدرُ هذه المقالة إلا ممَّنْ مُزِجَتْ معرفة الله تعالى بلحمه ودمه حتى تلاشى عندَهُ كلُّ ما سواه ، ولم يخف غيره ؟! وانظرْ قول النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : « إِنَّ عُمَرَ لَمُوقِنٌ )»، وهو الصادق المصدوقُ ، وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى [ النجم : ٣] وقال عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ في عثمان رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « إِنَّهُ لَتَسْتَحْيِي مِنْهُ مَلَائِكَةُ السَّمَاءِ »(۲) ورُوِيَ : أنَّه لم يكن يرفع رأسَهُ إلى السماءِ حياءً مِنَ اللهِ (۳) ؛ وذلك
May Allah be pleased with him immediately: 'Perhaps your brother left from the inheritance such and such.' And in one narration: He said to her: 'Perhaps your brother left besides you a wife, a mother, two daughters, and twelve brothers?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'That is your right; they did not wrong you.' (1) And examples like this that have been narrated from him are beyond count. So look at this sublime, holy perception by which difficult theoretical sciences became necessary for him. How is his perception of that for which the evidences have multiplied and the Quran and Hadith are filled with its proofs, and he was enamored with it and raised upon it from the time of his teething (2)? That is the knowledge of the Lord, mighty and majestic! Then, despite all this, he used to say about Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he died: 'Umar died as the most knowledgeable of us of Allah the Exalted.' And Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib said: 'I have not seen anyone more knowledgeable than Umar.' And in the Sahih: That the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, saw in a dream that he was drinking milk until the milk almost came out from his nails, and he gave the leftover of that milk to Umar, and the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, interpreted that dream as knowledge (3). And Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, was a kashif (possessor of unveiling); he would not estimate anything in his mind except that it occurred as if it were being drawn in the pure mirror of his mind, without evidence or indication. So how would his mind be for the knowledge of Him upon Whom all beings converge in clear indication, mighty and majestic?! And look at his saying, may Allah be pleased with him, when the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, informed him of the trial of the grave and the questioning of the two angels and their description, and he said: 'Will my intellect be with me?' He said: 'Yes, yes.' He said: 'Then I am sufficient for them both.' Then the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Indeed, Umar is certain.' (1) So look at his confidence, may Allah be pleased with him, in his intellect's reasoning and his disregard for debating those whose knowledge transcends from knowledge of certainty to eye of certainty—and they are the angels. And he did not fear that the terror of their appearance would occupy his mind, nor the atrocity of the grave, which is the first stage among the stages of the Hereafter. And such an utterance only emanates from one whose knowledge of Allah the Exalted has mixed with his flesh and blood such that everything else has vanished before him, and he feared none other than Him?! And look at the saying of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'Indeed, Umar is certain,' and he is the truthful and believed, and he does not speak from desire [Quran 53:3]. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said about Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Indeed, the angels of heaven are shy before him.' (2) And it has been narrated that he would not raise his head to the sky out of shyness from Allah (3); and that
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a panegyric demonstration of the extraordinary knowledge of Allah possessed by the Companion Umar ibn al-Khattab (رضي الله عنه). The author begins by recounting a story where Umar astutely deduced the inheritance shares of a woman's brother, showing his immediate and accurate knowledge without deliberation. The author comments that such instances are countless, and they illustrate a 'holy perception' that made difficult theoretical sciences intuitively necessary for him. The author then invites the reader to consider: if Umar could perceive matters that have abundant textual evidence so effortlessly, what must his knowledge of Allah be like? This is the main theme: Umar's marifa (knowledge of Allah) was of the highest order. The author then cites that Umar himself said at the death of the Prophet that he died 'the most knowledgeable of us of Allah,' and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib affirmed that he never saw anyone more knowledgeable than Umar. The author then references a prophetic dream in which milk symbolized knowledge, and the Prophet gave the leftover to Umar, indicating his superior share of knowledge. Next, the author states that Umar was a mukashaf (one endowed with unveiling): whatever he estimated in his mind would occur, as if manifested in the pure mirror of his mind, without need for evidence or indication. This is the point about kashf (unveiling) and intuitive knowledge. The author then asks rhetorically: if this was the case for worldly matters, how much more for knowledge of the Creator, Whose signs are clear in all beings? The author then presents the famous incident about the questioning in the grave: when the Prophet informed Umar about the trial of the grave and the angels Munkar and Nakir, Umar asked if his intellect ('aql) would be with him. When the Prophet affirmed, Umar said he would be sufficient for them. The Prophet then declared, 'Indeed, Umar is certain.' The author emphasizes Umar's trust in his intellect and his lack of fear despite the formidable situation. This shows his knowledge had reached the level of haqq al-yaqin (truth of certainty) or even 'ayn al-yaqin (eye of certainty). The author marvels that such a statement could only come from one whose knowledge of Allah was so integrated into his being that everything else ceased to matter. Finally, the author adds a related point about Uthman: the Prophet said the angels of heaven are shy before him, and it is narrated that Uthman would not raise his head to heaven out of shyness from Allah. This serves as further evidence of the profound knowledge and spiritual state of the Companions.

Key Terms

علوم نظرية
معرفة المولى
مكاشف
مرآة الذهن
علم اليقين
عين اليقين
موقن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that such intuitive knowledge means there is no need for intellectual effort or evidence.
Correction: The text shows that Umar's intuitive knowledge was a result of intense immersion in divine proofs and the Qur'an and Sunnah, not a replacement for them.

Checkpoint
What did Umar ask the Prophet regarding the questioning in the grave?
A) Will I be safe from punishment?
B) Will my intellect be with me?
C) Will the angels be gentle with me?
D) Can I avoid the trial?

Key Takeaway
Umar's certainty was so profound that he faced the angels of the grave with unwavering confidence, embodying the highest level of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Umar's knowledge of Allah mixed with his flesh and blood to the point that he faced the angels of the grave with unshakable confidence. Has your knowledge of Allah reached that depth? If not, what specific habit or study will you commit to today to move from theoretical belief to heartfelt certainty?
?
The Prophet testified, 'Indeed, Umar is certain.' Can you imagine the Prophet saying that about you? What would need to change in your daily life—your priorities, your fears, your attachments—for you to deserve such a testimony?
?
When Umar asked if his intellect would be with him in the grave, he trusted that his cultivated certainty would see him through. When you are alone in your grave, will your current level of faith suffice? If you are not certain, what will you do this week to strengthen your knowledge of Allah beyond mere intellectual assent?

Textual Proofs for the Sahaba's Excellence
Sanusi presents textual proofs for the Sahaba's knowledge and imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key textual proofs Sanusi uses to establish the high rank, firm knowledge, and imamate of the Companions.

Core Idea
The Sahaba's knowledge and imamate are proven by clear Qur'anic and prophetic testimony.

Sanusi now turns to proof texts to demonstrate the exalted status of the Companions. He presents a series of hadith and a Qur'anic verse that together show their certainty, their superiority not by outward acts but by inner faith, and their role as guides for all believers. This passage establishes that the Companions were not ordinary Muslims but divinely appointed leaders with the highest level of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without over-analyzing. Let the flow of proofs sink in.
The passage moves from fruit of watchfulness to specific hadith, then Quran, then general role.
2
Identify each proof
There are five distinct proofs: three hadith (Abu Bakr's certainty, his inner superiority, Umar's virtues), one Quranic verse, and the 'stars' hadith. Find each one in the text.
The hadith about Umar is presented as a question to Jibril.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why each proof is chosen. For example, the 'cover removed' hadith shows Abu Bakr's certainty is already perfect; the Quran verse shows divine testimony.
Sanusi calls the Quranic testimony 'great testimony from the King of kings'.
4
Connect to imamate and ijtihad
The last part explicitly states that the Companions are imams and references ijtihad. Consider how these proofs collectively establish their authority.
The 'stars' hadith is used as evidence for their imamate over all creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة المراقبة التي هي ثمرة كمال المعرفة ورسوخ اليقين ، حتى كأنَّهُ معاينة . وقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أبي بكرٍ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « لَوْ كُشِفَ الْغِطَاءُ عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرٍ .. مَا أَزْدَادَ يَقِيناً » وقالَ : « مَا فَضَلَكُمْ أَبُو بَكْرٍ بِكَثِيرِ صَلَاةٍ وَلَا صِيَامٍ ، وَإِنَّمَا فَضَلَكُمْ بِشَيْءٍ وَقَرَ فِي قَلْبِهِ » ورُوِيَ : أنَّ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ سال جبريل عليه السلام عن فضائل عمر رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ ، فقالَ : « لَوْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ مَا لَبِثَ نُوحٌ فِي قَوْمِهِ : أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَاماً .. مَا وَفَّيْتُ بِفَضَائِل عُمَرَ ، وَإِنَّهُ حَسَنَةٌ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ » وما عسى أنْ أعدَّ مِنْ محاسنِ الصحابة ومآثرهم ؟! ويكفي في رسوخ معارفهم وقُوَّةِ إيمانِهم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَأَلْزَمَهُمْ كَلِمَةَ التَّقْوَى وَكَانُوا أَحَقَّ بِهَا وَأَهْلَهَا ﴾ [الفتح : ٢٦] ، فانظر هذه الشهادة العظمى في حقهم ، الصادرة مِنْ ملك الملوك العالم بخفيَّاتِ الضَّمائر ويكفي في إمامتهم لجميع الخلْقِ - ولا يكون كذلكَ إِلا مَنْ بلغَ الرتبة العليا في الاجتهاد - قوله صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : « أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُومِ ؛ بِأَيْهِمْ أَقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ » ، وقد كانوا رضي الله عنهم متعرضين لدعاء الخلْقِ إلى الله تعالى ، وإقامةِ حُجَّةِ اللهِ تعالى جميع عليهم ، وإليهم المرجعُ في أزمنتهم في المسائلِ المُعضلة وجميع الحوادثِ النازلة
The fruit of watchfulness which is the fruit of perfection of knowledge and firmness of certainty, until he is as if seeing. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said about Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If the cover were removed from Abu Bakr, he would not increase in certainty.' And he said: 'Abu Bakr did not surpass you by much prayer or fasting, but he surpassed you by something that settled in his heart.' And it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked Jibril (peace be upon him) about the virtues of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and he said: 'If I remained among you as long as Noah remained among his people—a thousand years less fifty—I would not exhaust the virtues of Umar, and indeed he is a good deed among the good deeds of Abu Bakr.' And how can I count the good qualities and exploits of the Companions?! Sufficient for the firmness of their knowledge and the strength of their faith is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And He made them adhere to the word of piety, and they were most worthy of it and its people' [Al-Fath 26]; behold this great testimony in their favor, issued from the King of kings, Knower of the hidden secrets of consciences. And sufficient for their imamate over all creation—and it is not so except for one who has reached the highest rank of ijtihad—is the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'My Companions are like the stars; whichever of them you follow, you will be guided.' And they (may Allah be pleased with them) were engaged in calling creation to Allah Most High and establishing the proof of Allah Most High over all of them, and to them is the reference in their times in difficult issues and all occurring events.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a proof text in which Sanusi establishes the high rank and knowledge of the Companions (Sahaba) through textual evidence. He begins by describing the fruit of spiritual watchfulness as perfect knowledge and certainty, to the point of seeing reality directly. He then cites three prophetic hadiths: first, that Abu Bakr's certainty is so complete that even if the veil of the unseen were removed, it would increase him not; second, that Abu Bakr's superiority is not by outward acts but by a deep-seated inner faith; third, that Umar's virtues are so vast they cannot be enumerated, and he is a 'good deed' among Abu Bakr's good deeds. Sanusi then asks rhetorically how one can count the good qualities of the Companions. He then quotes the Quranic verse (48:26) as divine testimony to their firm knowledge and strong faith—Allah Himself praises them for adhering to 'the word of piety' and declares them worthy of it. Sanusi calls this a great testimony from the King of kings. Next, he presents the hadith that the Companions are like stars—whichever one you follow, you are guided—as proof of their imamate over all people, noting that this status requires the highest level of ijtihad. Finally, he describes the Companions' role as guides who call people to Allah and establish His proof, and as reference points for all difficult religious and worldly matters in their time.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Companions' knowledge was merely transmitted and not based on deep certainty.
Correction: The hadith and Quranic testimony show their knowledge was firm, certain, and divinely attested; for example, Abu Bakr's certainty would not increase even if the unseen were revealed.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, why did Abu Bakr surpass the other Companions?
A) Because of his many prayers and fasts.
B) Because of something that settled in his heart.
C) Because of his lineage.
D) Because of his wealth.

Key Takeaway
The Companions possess the highest level of certainty and knowledge, making them the rightful imams for all believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Abu Bakr's certainty was so complete that even the removal of the veil would not increase it. Sit with this: is your faith such that it would remain unmoved no matter what you saw or experienced? What illusion are you clinging to that a direct unveiling would shatter? Name one attachment you will surrender today to purify your certainty.
?
The Quran declares that the Companions were 'most worthy' of the word of piety. Do you live as if you believe that? Do you actually see them as your guides, or do you rely only on scholars? If their star is still meant to guide you, what would change if you took a Companion's approach to a current struggle in your life? Commit to one concrete action by the end of the week.
?
The Prophet said that Umar's virtues are so immense they cannot be enumerated even in a thousand years. How vast is your knowledge of the virtues of the Companions? Have you ever studied their lives with the intention of following their example? What excuse do you have for neglecting the very people Allah praised? Set a goal to read one biography of a Companion this month.

The Unique Light of the Prophet and the Definition of a Companion
Sanusi describes the Prophet's da'wah and defines a Companion based on his presence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the majority of scholars defined a Companion as anyone who met the Prophet believing in him, even briefly, and how the Prophet's unique light and method of da'wah made this possible.

Core Idea
A moment with the Prophet transforms even the coarsest person into a Companion.

Sanusi argues that the Prophet's da'wah was so effective that even a brief meeting with him had an immense transformative effect. This leads to a key theological definition: a Companion is not defined by length of association but by the special blessing of seeing the Prophet while believing. The passage combines a description of the Prophet's method, an analogy about teaching, and a definition that highlights the unique spiritual impact of his presence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow from the Prophet's da'wah to the definition of a Companion.
The passage includes a hadith at the end as evidence.
2
Identify the two main sections
The first part describes the Prophet's call and its effect; the second part defines a Sahabi based on that effect. Identify where the shift occurs.
The phrase 'ولهذا قال جمهور الأصوليين والمحدثين' marks the transition.
3
Reflect on the analogy and its conclusion
Sanusi compares ordinary teachers to the Prophet: if small teaching can remove blind imitation, how much more from the source of all lights? Understand how this supports the definition.
The analogy emphasizes the extraordinary blessing of even a moment with the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد دعا النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ جماعةً مِنْ حواشي الأعراب ، فطالبوه بالآية الدالة على صدقِهِ ، فأظهر لهم ما قامَتْ الحُجَّةُ به ، ولقد كانوا يفهمونَ الكلام العربي فهماً وافياً بالمعاني ، حاوياً لمقاصدِ الخطابِ ، والقرآنُ العظيم مملوء بالحُجَج والبراهين التي لا تُحصى كثرةً ، وقد أقامَ بينهمُ المُعلَّمُ الأكبر المبعوث لسياسة الخلق ، أفصحُ الخَلْقِ ، والمُعْطَى جوامع الكلام والشفقة التامة على عبادِ اللهِ ، صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .. ثلاث عشرة سنةً مِنْ غيرِ قتال يُوضّحُ الأدلَّةَ ، ويقيمُ الحُجَّةَ ، إلى أن ظهر الحق ظهوراً لم يبقَ معَهُ إِلا المعاندة معَ كمال المعرفةِ ، وبالنزر اليسيرِ مِنْ هذهِ المدَّةِ يحصل بتعليم الألكن وذي العِيِّ وقصور العقل مِنَ المعلمين للأبله والبليد مِنَ المتعلمينَ ما يخرجُ بهِ عنِ التقليدِ في عقائدِهِ خروجاً تاماً ، فكيف ترى حالَ مَنْ تلقَّى العلم مباشرةً ممَّنْ عمَّ نورُهُ البسيطة كلَّها ، بل مَنْ نوره أصلُ الأنوارِ كلَّها ، ومَنِ العقولُ كلُّها بالنسبة إلى عقلِهِ كَمَنْ أَخذَ حصاةً مِنْ رمال الدنيا كلّها ؟! على ما روى وهبُ بنُ منبِّهِ ولقد كانَ أجلفُ الأعرابِ يُسلِمُ ويشاهد طلعتهُ العليَّةَ ، فيُفيضُ مِنْ حينه برقائق العلومِ الجمَّةِ ، وغرائب الحِكَمِ الفاخرة ، ويَرِقُ طبعُهُ ، وتتهذَّبُ أخلاقُهُ مِنْ فورِهِ ، ولهذا قال جمهورُ الأصوليين والمحدثينَ : إِنَّ الصحابي : هو مَنِ اجتمعَ مؤمناً معَ النبيِّ صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ وإنْ لم يرو عنه ، وإنْ لم تَطُلْ صحبتُهُ لهُ ، مع أنَّ هذا القَدْرَ لا يُحصِّلُ الصحبة في حقٌّ غيرِهِ لغةً ولا عُرْفاً ! وما ذلكَ إِلا لِمَا عرفتَ مِنْ أنَّ اللحظةَ مِنْ مشاهدتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ يَحصُلُ بها مِنَ الأنوار والبركاتِ ما لا يُقدَرُ على حضره ، ويغيب في نورِ تلك اللحظة أنوار العلماء كلهم. روى الدارمي ( ١٦ ) ، والبيهقي في ( الاعتقاد » ( ١٤ ) عن سيدنا ابن عباس الله عنهما قال : جاء أعرابي إلى النبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فقال : بِمَ أعرف أنك رسول الله ؟ فقال : « أرأيتَ لو دعوتُ هذا العِدْقَ مِنْ هذهِ النخلة . . أتشهد أنّي رسولَ اللهِ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : فدعا العذق ، فجعل العذق ينزل من النخلة حتى سقط الأرض . . . الحديث
The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, indeed called a group of the outlying Bedouins, and they demanded from him the sign indicating his truthfulness, so he showed them that by which the proof was established. And they understood the Arabic speech with a full understanding of the meanings, encompassing the purposes of the discourse. And the Great Quran is filled with arguments and proofs whose abundance cannot be counted. And the Greatest Teacher, sent to manage the creation, the most eloquent of creation, given the comprehensive speech and complete compassion towards the servants of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, established among them for thirteen years without fighting, clarifying the evidences and establishing the proof, until the truth appeared in a way that left nothing but obstinacy with complete knowledge. And in a very small portion of this period, through teaching of the mute and the slow and those of deficient intellect from the teachers to the dull and stupid from the learners, one obtains that which takes him completely out of blind imitation in his beliefs. So what do you think of the state of one who received knowledge directly from him whose light encompassed the entire earth? Indeed, his light is the source of all lights, and all intellects compared to his intellect are like one who took a pebble from all the sands of the world? According to what Wahb ibn Munabbih narrated: And indeed the coarsest Bedouin would accept Islam and witness his lofty countenance, and immediately pour forth abundant subtle sciences and precious strange wisdoms, and his nature would soften, and his character would be refined instantly. Because of this, the majority of the usuliyyun (fundamental scholars) and muhaddithun (hadith scholars) said: The Companion is whoever met the Prophet believing in him, even if he did not narrate from him, and even if his companionship was not long, although this amount does not yield companionship for anyone else linguistically or customarily! And that is only because you know that a moment of seeing him, peace and blessings be upon him, obtains from lights and blessings that cannot be valued, and in the light of that moment the lights of all scholars disappear. Narrated by al-Darimi (16) and al-Bayhaqi in al-I'tiqad (14) from our master Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: A Bedouin came to the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, and said: By what do I know that you are the Messenger of Allah? He said: 'Do you see, if I call this cluster from this palm tree... would you testify that I am the Messenger of Allah?' He said: Yes. He said: So he called the cluster, and the cluster began to descend from the palm tree until it fell to the ground... the hadith.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a combined argument and definition. The author first describes the Prophet's method of da'wah: he called a group of Bedouins who demanded a miracle, and he provided clear proof. The Prophet spent thirteen years without warfare, clarifying evidences until the truth was so manifest that only obstinacy remained. The author then makes an analogy: if even a little teaching from ordinary teachers can take a dull student out of blind imitation in his beliefs, then how immense must be the effect of learning directly from the Prophet whose light is the source of all lights and whose intellect dwarfs all others? He then cites a report from Wahb ibn Munabbih that even the coarsest Bedouin would become refined immediately upon seeing the Prophet. Based on this, the majority of scholars defined a Sahabi as anyone who met the Prophet believing in him, even briefly and even if he did not narrate, because the unique blessing of that moment cannot be achieved through any other means. The footnote provides a specific miracle: the Prophet called a date cluster from a palm tree as a sign for a Bedouin.

الصحابي
الأصوليون
المحدثون
المعاندة
التقليد
الأنوار
أجلف الأعراب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A Companion must have a long period of association or must have narrated many hadiths.
Correction: The passage states that a mere moment of seeing the Prophet while believing suffices because of the unique light and blessings of that meeting.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of a Companion (Sahabi) according to the majority of scholars?
A) Anyone who met the Prophet for a long time
B) Anyone who met the Prophet believing in him, even briefly and without narrating
C) Anyone who narrated many hadiths
D) Anyone who was related to the Prophet

Key Takeaway
A Companion is defined by the transformative blessing of meeting the Prophet while believing, regardless of the duration or narration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have access to the Quran and Sunnah every day, yet the Bedouin was transformed in one glimpse of the Prophet. Why does your heart remain unchanged despite constant exposure? What one excuse will you drop today to seek that transformation?
?
The Prophet's light is the source of all lights. Are you dazzled by the lights of scholars, influencers, or your own intellect more than by his example? How will you intentionally recenter your spiritual focus on him starting this prayer?
?
If a single moment with the Prophet made a coarse Bedouin a Companion, what does it say about your own faith that you still wrestle with basic obedience after years of being a Muslim? What will you do today to let the Prophet's message penetrate your heart as it did theirs?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Definition of a Companion and the Effect of Seeing the Prophet
Sanusi defines the sahabi and explains the effect of seeing the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a companion (sahabi) as accepted by the majority of scholars and the reason why a brief encounter with the Prophet suffices.

Core Idea
A single moment in the Prophet's presence transforms a person into a companion.

This lesson explores a fascinating aspect of Islamic biographical literature: the definition of a companion. Sanusi presents a compelling argument that even a rough Bedouin, upon seeing the Prophet, was so profoundly affected that he became a repository of knowledge and refined character. This leads to the scholarly consensus that anyone who met the Prophet in faith, even briefly, is a companion. The underlying reason is the unique spiritual radiance of the Prophet, which eclipses all other lights.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage and Translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
The passage begins with a rhetorical question.
2
Identify the Example
Sanusi uses the example of a rough Bedouin who becomes refined upon seeing the Prophet. Notice the description of transformation.
3
Understand the Definition
The scholars define a companion as anyone who met the Prophet in faith, even without narrating or prolonged association. Note that this definition is unique to the Prophet.
Compare with ordinary usage of 'companion'.
4
Grasp the Rationale
The reason is the immense spiritual lights and blessings from the Prophet's presence. Even a moment of seeing him surpasses all other knowledge.
Reflect on the phrase 'the lights of all scholars become dim'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مِنْ رمال الدنيا كلّها ؟! على ما روى وهبُ بنُ منبِّهِ ولقد كان أجلف الأعراب يُسلِمُ ويشاهد طلعته العليَّةَ ، فيُفيضُ مِنْ حينه برقائق العلومِ الجمَّةِ ، وغرائب الحِكَمِ الفاخرة ، ويَرِقُ طبعُهُ ، وتتهذَّبُ أخلاقُهُ مِنْ فورِهِ ، ولهذا قال جمهورُ الأصوليين والمحدثينَ : إِنَّ الصحابي : هو مَنِ اجتمعَ مؤمناً معَ النبيِّ صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ وإنْ لم يرو عنه ، وإنْ لم تَطُلْ صحبتُهُ لهُ ، مع أنَّ هذا القَدْرَ لا يُحصِّلُ الصحبة في حقٌّ غيرِهِ لغةً ولا عُرْفاً ! وما ذلكَ إِلا لِمَا عرفتَ مِنْ أنَّ اللحظةَ مِنْ مشاهدتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ يَحصُلُ بها مِنَ الأنوار والبركاتِ ما لا يُقدَرُ على حضره ، ويغيب في نورِ تلك اللحظة أنوار العلماء كلهم
From the sands of the world entirely?! According to what Wahb ibn Munabbih narrated: and indeed the most uncouth of the Bedouins would accept Islam and witness his lofty countenance, then immediately flow with abundant subtleties of knowledge and exquisite wisdoms, and his nature would become refined and his morals disciplined instantly. For this reason the majority of usul scholars and hadith scholars said: The Companion (al-ṣaḥābī) is whoever met the Prophet (peace be upon him) in faith, even if he did not narrate from him and even if his companionship was not long, although this measure does not achieve companionship (ṣuḥba) for others linguistically or customarily! And that is only because, as you know, a moment of seeing him (peace be upon him) brings such lights and blessings that cannot be estimated, and in the light of that moment the lights of all scholars become dim.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of the term 'companion' (ṣaḥābī) and explains its rationale. The author begins by recounting an example: even a rough Bedouin, upon seeing the Prophet, immediately acquires refined knowledge and character. This is evidence that a brief encounter with the Prophet has immense spiritual effect. Therefore, the majority of scholars define a companion as any believer who met the Prophet, even without prolonged association or narration. This definition is unique to the Prophet; for others, such a brief meeting would not constitute companionship linguistically or customarily. The reason is that the Prophet's presence radiates divine lights and blessings that overshadow all other knowledge, such that even a single moment of seeing him transforms a person.

Key Terms
الصحابي
الصحبة
الأنوار
البركات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A companion must have spent a long time with the Prophet and narrated many hadith.
Correction: The majority of scholars hold that even a single meeting in faith, without long association or narration, qualifies one as a companion.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of usul and hadith scholars, what is the definition of a companion (sahabi)?
A) Anyone who lived during the Prophet's time
B) Anyone who met the Prophet in faith, even if briefly and without narrating hadith
C) Anyone who narrated at least one hadith
D) Anyone who was a Muslim for at least one year

Key Takeaway
The status of being a companion is granted by faith and a single meeting with the Prophet, due to the extraordinary spiritual effulgence of his presence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The rough Bedouin was instantly transformed upon seeing the Prophet. You have access to the Prophet's words and example through the Qur'an and Sunnah. Why do you not experience that same immediate transformation? What barrier stands between you and the light of his sunnah? Commit to removing that barrier today.
?
If a single moment with the Prophet granted the status of a companion, would you trade all your years of knowledge and deeds for that one moment? Let your answer reveal whether you truly value his presence over everything else. What change will you make to prioritize seeking his company (through his legacy) over worldly distractions?
