Seven People Named Muhammad
Sanusi lists seven companions named Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific set of seven companions who shared the name Muhammad during the Prophet's lifetime and the importance of their identification.

Core Idea
Seven companions named Muhammad: a unique group from the early Muslim community.

This passage from Sanusi’s work presents a historical note: a list of seven companions who were given the name Muhammad near the time of his birth. Such lists serve to preserve the names of those who bore the Prophet’s name in his own era, highlighting the careful record-keeping of early Islamic biography. As you read, pay attention to the detailed genealogical and phonetic notes that ensure each person is correctly identified.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice that the author first states the exception and then enumerates the seven names.
The passage includes detailed pronunciation guides in parentheses.
2
Count the names
Identify each of the seven names listed. They are introduced with 'and' or 'and Muhammad' – try to list them in order.
The author explicitly says 'their number is seven'.
3
Observe the phonetic glosses
Notice that for some names, Sanusi provides vowel markings and letter details. This is to ensure correct pronunciation and avoid confusion between similar names.
For example, 'Uhayha' has specific vowel markings.
4
Reflect on the historical context
Think about why such a list would be important. It shows the care taken to preserve the identities of those who shared the Prophet’s name, and it reflects the early community's respect for the name Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أُناساً قليلين تسموا قريباً مِنْ مولده باسمه ( عددهم سبعة : محمد بن مسلمة الأنصاري ، ومحمدُ بنُ أُحَيْحَةَ بنِ الجُلاح - بضم الهمزة وحاءين مهملتين مفتوحتين بينهما يا ساكنة ، والجُلاحُ : بضم الجيم ولام مخففة وآخرُهُ حاء مهملة - ومحمد بن براء البكري بتخفيف الراء ، ومحمد بن سفيانَ بنِ مجاشع ، ومحمدُ بنُ حُمْرانَ الجُعفيُّ ، ومحمدُ بنُ خزاعة السلمي ، ومحمدُ بنُ اليَحْمدي بفتح الياء وضم الميم وفتحها (٢) .
Except for a few people who were named after him close to his birth. Their number is seven: Muhammad ibn Maslama al-Ansari, and Muhammad ibn Uhayha ibn al-Julah - with a damma on the hamza and two open ha' between them a silent ya, and al-Julah: with a damma on the jim and a lightened lam and its end is a ha - and Muhammad ibn Bara' al-Bakri with a lightened ra', and Muhammad ibn Sufyan ibn Mujashi', and Muhammad ibn Humran al-Ju'fi, and Muhammad ibn Khaza'a al-Sulami, and Muhammad ibn al-Yahmadi with a fatha on the ya and a damma on the mim and a fatha on it (2).
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list. The author enumerates seven companions who shared the name Muhammad during the Prophet's lifetime, providing their full names with careful phonological glosses to ensure correct pronunciation and identification. This list serves as a historical note within the broader discussion of prophethood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This list includes all companions named Muhammad.
Correction: The passage explicitly says 'except for a few people' and lists seven; it is not an exhaustive list.

Checkpoint
How many people named Muhammad are listed in this passage?
A) 4
B) 5
C) 6
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Seven companions named Muhammad are listed by Sanusi as a historical record of those who bore the Prophet's name in his own time.

Closing Supplication and Colophon
Closing supplication and colophon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional closing formulas used by scholars in classical commentaries and the author's humble supplication for himself and his readers.

Core Idea
A scholar's work ends not with pride, but with humble prayer for guidance and forgiveness.

Sanusi concludes his commentary with a heartfelt supplication. This closing passage reveals the author's piety and his hope that the work benefits those who study it. It also reflects the traditional practice of ending scholarly works with prayers and salutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic supplication once without analyzing. Then read the literal English translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the repetition of 'Amen' and the formal closing phrases.
2
Identify the three main requests
The author asks for himself (faith, forgiveness, paradise), for readers of his work (understanding, good seal, purity), and ends with salutations on the Prophet and all prophets.
3
Reflect on the humility and tradition
Consider why a scholar would end with such a prayer rather than self-congratulation. This reflects the Islamic emphasis on sincerity and reliance on Allah.
This connects to the core idea.
4
Note the textual peculiarity
The phrase 'اسم مدرب العالمين' is likely a scribal error for 'الحمد لله رب العالمين'. Recognize that manuscripts sometimes have such issues.
This is a minor textual note, not a doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا أوان الفراغ مِنْ هذا التعليق المباركِ إِنْ شاءَ الله تعالى ، فنسأله سبحانَهُ أَنْ يَختم لنا بالإيمان والإسلام ، واتباع السنة ، والمغفرة لجميع ذنوبنا بلا محنة في الدنيا ولا في الآخرة ، وأنْ يبوثنا معَ الآباء والأمَّهاتِ والإخوة والذريَّةِ والأحبَّةِ مِنْ أعالي الفردوس المنازل الفاخرة ، وأنْ يُسهل الفهم على كلِّ مَنْ تعاطى هذا الشرحَ أو أصله ، ويختم له بخواتم السعداء ، ويشرح صدره ، ويُزَكِّيَ في الدنيا والآخرة فعله وقولَهُ ، آمين آمين آمين يا رب العالمين . والصلاة والسلام على سيّد الأولين والآخرينَ ، ورضي الله تعالى عن آلِهِ وصحبهِ ومَنْ تبعهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين ، وسلام على جميع النبيين والمرسلين وآخر دعوانا أن اسم مدرب العالمين ولاحول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلی العظيم
And this is the time of completion of this blessed commentary, if Allah wills. So we ask Him—glorified is He—to conclude for us with faith and Islam, following the Sunna, forgiveness for all our sins without trial in this world or the Hereafter; and to settle us with fathers, mothers, brothers, offspring, and beloved ones in the lofty abodes of Paradise; and to facilitate understanding for everyone who engages with this commentary or its original, and to seal him with the seals of the fortunate, and to expand his breast, and to purify in this world and the Hereafter his deed and his saying. Amen, amen, amen, O Lord of the worlds. And prayers and peace be upon the master of the first and the last, and may Allah be pleased with his family, his companions, and those who follow them in excellence until the Day of Judgment. And peace be upon all the prophets and messengers. And the conclusion of our call is that [?] the name of the trainer of the worlds, and there is no power nor strength except by Allah, the Most High, the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage is the author's closing supplication and colophon for his commentary. He thanks Allah for completion and asks for a good end, forgiveness, and to be gathered with loved ones in Paradise. He also prays for those who use his work, that they gain understanding and righteousness. He ends with salutations on the Prophet, his family, companions, and all prophets, and a standard closing phrase. The specific phrase 'اسم مدرب العالمين' appears to be a corruption of the usual 'الحمد لله رب العالمين' (Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds). This passage shows the author's humility and traditional closing formulas.

Key Terms
تعليق
خواتم السعداء
شرح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Scholarly works often end with the author boasting about their achievement.
Correction: Instead, Sanusi ends with humble supplication, acknowledging Allah's grace and seeking forgiveness and guidance for himself and his readers.

Checkpoint
What does the author ask for those who engage with his commentary?
A) Wealth and fame.
B) Understanding, a good seal, an expanded breast, and purification of deed and saying.
C) Long life and many students.
D) Victory over enemies.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's closing supplication shows his humility and his hope that his commentary brings benefit and guidance to its readers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you complete a project or study, do you end with humble prayer for forgiveness and guidance, or do you feel self-congratulation? What would it look like for you to adopt the author's attitude in your own work?
?
The author prays for everyone who will engage with his commentary. Are you mindful of the lasting impact of your words and actions? How can you ensure that what you leave behind benefits others sincerely?
?
You ask Allah for a good end (seals of the fortunate). Are you living today in a way that you would be content to meet your Lord? If not, what is one concrete change you will make starting now?
